Sometimes there is a rupture in the ankles, as we have said, and you should elevate the area.
And do not leave any cause of intestines in the groin; and if they do, it is little; and it returns at all hours.
But if the time is prolonged with this, a fissure is adjusted in the groin until the intestine descends into the groin; and this happens due to the extension of the groin, which is in the ankles, as we have said, which causes the groin to be stretched, and subsequently softened, and the area becomes suppurated and elevated.
And the cure for it is with cautery, as is preceded by the narration of it.
And sometimes it is cured with an iron following this method:  and it is that the patient lies on their back between your hands, and then dry the area of the rupture of the suppurating swelling with cauterization by incision to a width according to the quantity of three days.
And then, pull the white groin area, which is under the hip, until it is exposed.
And then take the reed and place it on the prominent area of the groin, and press it against the belly button.
And then stitch the two prominent areas on the extremity of the groin's reed, and join one of them to the other with the suture.
And then remove the extremity of the reed, and do not sever the groin completely, nor extend the testicles, nor any other such thing, as I have shown you in the treatment of intestinal hernia.
And then treat it with the treatment for sores, and as you would cut away the pus, cleanse it and restore the sore until it is healed; for the groin is contracted, and the prominence of the rupture is not adjusted.
And cauterization is better in this location, for it is more conducive to health.
Chapter 68.
Of the softening of the swelling of the testicles.
Often the swelling of the testicles in some men is softened in this way, because the flesh around it is softened, and care is taken of it.
Therefore, it is necessary for the one who is engaged in its treatment to have the patient lie according to his side, and gently spread all the softened swelling over the natural swelling; and then to draw together the two edges with sutures.
And if you wish, stitch the excess of the softened swelling at the beginning with three or four stitches, and with firm sutures.
And then, cut between the sutures; and then treat it by treating the other sores until it is healed and the pus comes out.
Chapter 69.
Of castration.
Know that castration, in our law, is forbidden, but because of the reasons given to me, I am obliged to mention it in this book; and it is not necessary to remember it except in two ways.  One is so that when a physician is questioned about it, he will know how to treat whatever happens to him; and the other is that we often have need of castrating other animals for our benefit, just as we do with oxen, goats, pigs, and animals of similar kind.
And therefore I say that castration is done in two ways: either by crushing, or by slitting and cutting.
But in the method of castration by crushing, the way to operate is to immerse the animal in hot water until its genitals are softened and relaxed and hang down. And then take them with your hand until they are broken and no longer appear beneath the touch.
But in castration performed by slitting and cutting, you must hold the animal and press the scrotum with your left hand.
Then tie the suspensory ligament, and cut into each testicle with a cut until both testicles are removed.
And then cut those further, once you've skinned each one. And do not leave any cause on those of the scrotum, but only the thin scrotum that is over the vessels.
And this method of castration is better, which is done by attrition, because strong attrition leaves no cause in the testicles for the animal to desire mating.
And then treat the wound until it is healed.
Chapter 70.
Of the treatment of hermaphroditism.
Hermaphroditism in men occurs in two ways: one is when there appears in the scrotum area, in the space between the testicles, a figure resembling a woman's vulva, with hair in it.
And sometimes urine flows from the area between the testicles.
But in women, there is one type:  the woman's vulva on her pubic region is like two testicles of a man somewhat diminished at the outer edge, similar to the foreskin of a man, and two testicles.
And the treatment is of three types: for two of the men's types and one type of the women's. And it is necessary that you cut those adhering flesh until the swelling subsides, and then treat them with the treatment for other sores.
And in the second type for men, where urine is in the groin area around the testicles, there is no treatment or operation for it.
Chapter 21.
Of tumors and prominent flesh due to women's causes.
A mild tumor, adhering to natural causes, until it is squeezed and made smooth, is observed; and sometimes it is magnified in some women to the point of spreading just like in men and preventing intercourse.
Then you should hold the excess tumor with your hand or forceps and cut it.
And do not overdo the cutting, especially at the root of the tumor, so that you do not cause a flood of blood.
And then treat it with the treatment for sores until it is healed.
But a fleshy growth is a flesh that grows within the womb of the mother until it fills it, and easily extends to the outside parts like a tail (and thus some earlier ones called this 'tail disease'); therefore, we must cut it as we cut a tumor, and treat it until it is healed.
Chapter 72.
Of the treatment of elephantiasis.
Elephantiasis is when the vaginal opening of a woman is not perforated, or is very small. And it is either natural or accidental.
Accidental is due to an illness that has preceded it, and that illness is caused either by poorly fitting flesh, or by a subtle or thick cicatrix.
And it is formed either on the mother's womb, or on her ribs, or on the highest part of her body, or the lowest, and you prohibit coitus, pregnancy, and childbirth, and strongly prohibit menstruation.
And the knowledge of this is obtained by observing the woman; if the obstruction is evident, treat it promptly. But if it is not apparent, then you search for it with your probing or with a ray (likely a medical instrument).
But if the obstruction is due to a thin cicatrix, and is close to the two lips, then you should cut and break it open.
And you should place powders on the two lips, and then place your index fingers of both hands upon them.
And the woman should be on her back, her thighs spread, and then forcefully extend the two lips until that thin cicatrix is broken and the obstruction is opened.
And then take wool and soak it in oil, and place it over the area, and let the patient lie down with a man for the day, so that the incised area does not heal.
But if the cicatrix is thick and large, then it is necessary that you cut it with a sharp knife or a myrtle leaf.
But if the obstruction is due to flesh, then suspend it with forceps, and cut it.
And have with you medicines that stop blood flow without causing a bite, such as acacia, dragon's blood, and alum, mixed with egg white.
And then administer a wide lead cannula so that the wound does not heal too quickly.
And keep that in place for several days and apply poultices of dried herbs.
And then treat it with other healing methods of consolidation until it is healed.
And sometimes it extends to the surrounding flesh, and then it is necessary to cut it according to this method. But if it is due to a brain abscess, a brain abscess which is in the head should not be treated with iron in any way.
Chapter 73.
Of the treatment of hemorrhoids, and of the tail and red swelling that occurs in the vagina of women.
Hemorrhoids are understood as the openings of many veins through which a lot of blood continuously flows; and when these hemorrhoids are longstanding and inflamed.
And I have already mentioned in the division the types of these [hemorrhoids] and their symptoms, and I will now explain which ones receive treatment and which ones do not.
Therefore, I say that hemorrhoids and inflammations, when they are deep within the anus and do not appear outwardly, then treatment with iron should not be attempted for them.
But those which are at the opening of the anus, where you can feel them, are those which can be treated.
And you should place the woman in a cool place and then carefully cut the inflammation with shears, or with a rough cloth, and cut those inflamed areas at their roots.
And then sprinkle over those areas the flow of blood from one of the incisive powders without a mordant, such as acacia and similar ones.
And then soak their feet for an hour, and then place them in cool water.
And if the flow of blood persists, then place it in a decoction of pomegranate seeds and bark, and similar things.
And then take barley flour and mix it with honey and sour wine, and make a poultice with this and place it on their back.
And if the blood is separated, it is good; and if not, apply two cupping glasses, to the breasts without making incisions.
And then take wool and soak it in coriander juice, or arnica juice, or agrimony juice with diluted wine, and apply it to the area; and then treat the area with ointments until it is healed.
And treat that until it is healed.
Chapter 74.
Concerning the accidental piercing of the breast.
Many kinds of abscesses occur in the breast, such as cancer, stony abscesses, ulcers, inflamed swellings, eruptions, fistulas, hemorrhoids, sores, and other abscesses. And I have already described these diseases and their types, and their signs, and their cures in the division.
And it is necessary that I describe in this treatise the hot abscess which comes in the breast when it is of the abscesses that collects pus, and if you wish to know in what way the operation of it is done with iron.
Then you must consider if the pain of the abscess at its beginning is sharp with throbbing, phlegm, and fever, and if there is redness and if you feel the pus, then do not hurry with piercing it, and treat it with what aids in maturation until the sharpness of the symptoms subsides.
And then you must have the woman lie down on a bed with two mattresses; and lean her on her two sides and draw her feet towards the lower part of her belly, and spread her thighs, and place her arms under her temples, and bind each one with a bandage suitable for it.
And then the midwife, standing on the right side, administers the instrument with which the opening in the breast is made, the shape of which will be apparent in those things that will be done next.
And when you want to administer this instrument, you must insert its tip into the nipple of the woman's breast, and what enters the breast with the instrument should be no more than the nipple, and comfort the patient. But if the instrument is larger than the nipple, then you must place powders on the nipple's surface to prevent any instrument from entering the nipple.
And you should place the lubricant that is on the instrument on the upper side, and the attendant should hold the instrument and rotate the lubricant until the opening of the breast is opened.
And when the discharge appears, and it is touched with the hand and is yellowish and moist, then you must dry that area around his head with a linen cloth.
And when the discharge is evacuated, then you should place a piece of cloth soaked in rubbed oil or green oil (in which there is some astringent substance) on the affected area, and place the compress on the nipple's region.
And place over the breast, and on the surrounding area, a clean wool cloth soaked in water in which mallows have been boiled.
And it should be treated for approximately two days with the ointment that is appropriate for this until it is healed.
And sometimes the breast and the affected area are washed in a way that is cleansed with water and honey, and then with water in which lily root or long-stemmed iris has been boiled, and then return to the ointment.
And if the affected area is deep within the breast, then you should be prohibited from treating it with iron, having treated it with what we have mentioned in the section.
Chapter 75.
To teach the midwives how to treat living infants when their bodies are not formed naturally.
It is necessary for the midwife to know, at the beginning, the natural form of childbirth through its signs.  When you see the woman straining downwards, and she desires to breathe air, and is relieved by what is upon her in childbirth, and hastens the delivery of the infant, then know that this birth is according to the natural form. The delivery of the infant is upon its head, and the afterbirth with it, either suspended or hanging from the navel.
Therefore, when you see these signs, the woman's abdomen should be compressed so that the infant descends easily. For when it descends upon its head, it leaves the afterbirth, which is cleansed of those superfluities with good cleaning.
But that which is different from this birth is unnatural and undesirable, for when the infant emerges feet first and its body comes out before its head and feet, or one hand, or one foot, or its head, or its hand or belly, and the head is turned to its neck forcefully and resembles other undesirable shapes.
Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be knowledgeable and skillful in all these matters, and to guard against error and deception.
And I am showing all the forms of these, and what ingenuity is in them so that it is signified by this and be stated about it.
When the birth is accomplished upon its head through natural progression, and this is difficult for the woman and her powers are weakened, then have the women hold the child, and evaporate the child's heat with collected fenugreek and moist oils.
And now the midwife should gently insert her fingers into the small space or cleft and with that detach the afterbirth, or cut it with her fingernail until she removes the moisture within it. And press the woman's abdomen until the fetus descends.
But if it does not descend, then it is necessary that the woman be treated with poultices of plantain and fenugreek with cumin.
And now command him, now the one applying the poultice, to be firm and make the woman sneeze with force; and hold her mouth and nostrils for one hour, for the fetus will be expelled soon.
And if the two hands of the fetus are expelled at the beginning, then you must gently return them little by little. But if you do not succeed in the procedure, then place the woman on a table and lift her feet up, and then lower the table onto the ground; and the woman should be held so she does not fall during the action.
And if the hands are not returned and the fetus dies, then cut them and remove the remaining part of the fetus or tie the body to the woman's hand with a cloth and remove it evenly, for it will be expelled.
When the fetus is on its feet, then you must push them upwards, and then turn the fetus gently, and then cradle it, and then take one of its feet and extend it gently.
But when it has emerged between the thighs, then you instruct it to strain, and make it cough with force, for it will be expelled if God wills it.
And if it is not expelled with what we have recounted, then you return the fetus little by little until you place it in its natural position, for it will then be expelled with an easy delivery.
And if it is not expelled with all that we have recounted, then take marshmallow and dissolved gum, and pound it well in a mortar, and then apply it to the vagina of the woman, to the lower part of her abdomen. And then apply a poultice in lukewarm water, until the hypochondria (the lower ribs and sides of the abdomen) are eased.
And when the lower parts of the body are soothed, then apply a fumigation of myrtle and place it over the patient. And when the fumigation has been applied for an hour, then you place it on a linen cloth, and then make the person sneeze and press their mouth shut, and remove the cloth and apply gentle pressure to the lower abdomen, for the fetus will soon be expelled.
Expulsion of the fetus lengthwise while one of her hands is used. Be resourceful in reducing the [fetus's] hand, but if you cannot reduce it, then lift the woman and make her walk.
And if walking is not possible, then have her lie down on the bed, and forcefully squeeze her thighs, and then administer medicines that I have recommended, made from mucilages.
And if labor has begun, then have her sit on a stool, and then consider the reduction of the hand, and gently guide the fetus into its natural position, and make the woman sneeze and command her to push until it is expelled.
The fetus is on the mother's pelvis, its hands and face are turned towards its mother's back. The midwife should grasp the fetus's hand and gently, little by little, turn it, and remove it with ease.
And when it is positioned correctly, then apply to its navel what we have recommended of oil and mucilages.
And then command her to gently cough, and when you have done this, have her sit on a stool and command her to lean to her right side, and then command her to push; and make her sneeze with condiments. The prepared fetus is delivered on its side.
When the mother is delivered of the horrific thing (likely referring to the afterbirth) in this manner, consider it, and then you cut the afterbirth with your fingernail until it is emptied of moisture.
And if the fetus is suspended by the face and neck, then you cut the umbilical cord so that it is not retained and dies.
And then push the fetus towards the parts inside until you have positioned it correctly, and instruct the woman to push a few times, and it will be expelled easily, if God wills it.
Delivery of twins or multiple fetuses. Know that twins are often born, and sometimes three or four, but this is unusual and rarely happens; but these are things outside the natural order, and not living.  (This last part is a bit ambiguous and potentially referring to deformed or non-viable infants)
And count those, whether they are multiple, as a single set, and separate them by their umbilical cords.  And sometimes they are expelled as easily as one fetus through natural means, and sometimes through unnatural means, as we have recounted.
And if some of them are difficult to deliver and fall into what we have described as unnatural occurrences, then treat them as we have recounted.
And if the midwife is skillful and does this with ease and subtlety, and with patience, and is ingenious according to every figure, according to what is prepared for her by the skillful attendant to bring about health.
A recollection of what is formed in the womb from embryos and miscarriages.
Sometimes one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, or even ten are formed in the mother's womb, and it has already been verified by me that one woman miscarried six, and another ten, all formed.  The cause of this was determined by the learned wise.
And all this should be within the midwife's knowledge, for it is easily perceived by someone similar to her, and therefore she should apply herself to it accordingly.
Chapter 76.
Of the extraction of the fetus when it is dead.
When you treat the dead fetus with what we have said in the division of the treatment, and it has not come out, and you are forced to use manual operation, then you must consider whether the woman is of sound constitution and is not afflicted by any of the conditions that cause concern for her loss.
Then the woman should be positioned on the bed on her back, with her head tilted downwards and her thighs elevated.
And the attendant should hold either both sides or bind her to the bed so that her body does not move during the extraction of the fetus.
And then you should moisten the mother's mouth with moist oils and with mucilage of marshmallow, fenugreek, and linseed.
And then the midwife should anoint her hand with those oils and mucilages, and then gently insert her hand into the mother, and then seek with her hand the place where she can hook her fingernails into the fetus.
And suitable places for this: then consider if the fetus is ready to descend onto its head, and then you should hook your fingernails into its neck, or into its jaw, or into its mouth, or into its palate, or under its chin, or into its armpits, or into the appropriate places on the sides, or under the ribs.
But if the descent is on its feet, then in the groin, or in the middle of the back.
And it is necessary to hold the fingernail with the right hand, and to place its curve in that place which is between the fingers of the left hand, and to gently insert the hand and hook the fingernail into any of those places we have mentioned, until it reaches the empty space.
And then place another fingernail, or a third if necessary, in its vicinity, so that there is a pulling, not a stretching according to its natural state alone.
And it should be moved in all directions, so that its removal is eased just as is done in a tooth removal.
And it is necessary in that which is between them that the stretching be softened; and if any part of it is retained, then it is necessary for the midwife to anoint some of her fingers with oil, and insert those fingers and twist with them that which is retained.
Therefore, if the part of the fet is expelled, then the fingernails should be moved to a higher location; and do this until all of the fet is expelled.
But if the hand is pulled out ahead of the other, and it is not possible to return it by constricting it, then it is necessary that a cloth be wrapped around it; and then pull it out until it is completely expelled, and cut it either at the joint of the hand or at the elbow.
And thus it is necessary that you do the same for the other hand and the two feet.
But if the head of the fet is large, or constriction happens during its expulsion, or water is collected in its head, then it is necessary to insert fingers between the ribs and split the head and remove the water, or to cut it with an instrument called "alundat," the shape of which will be shown with the other instruments in the chapter following this one.
And similarly, do this if the fet is naturally large-headed: and then it is necessary to cut it with *algematu* (or something else), or to grasp it with *alunda* as we have said; and then remove the bones with forceps.
And if the head is expelled and is constricted towards the fork (furcula), then it should be split until the moisture which is in its feet is discharged.
But if it is not complicated, nor obstructing the expulsion, then you cut the head as soon as possible.
And if the lower part of the abdomen is abscess-ridden or dropsical, then you must pierce it until the moisture within it runs out.
But if the fet is on its feet, then the traction on it is gentle and the direction of it towards the mother's mouth is gentle.
But if it is constricted towards the belly and the feet, then you must extract it with a cloth that you will have wrapped around your hand, and split the belly and feet until what is within them runs out.
But if the other limbs are removed and the head remains, then the midwife inserts her left hand; but if the mother's mouth is open, then she inserts her hand into the air space, and searches for the head with it, and pulls it with her fingers towards the mother's mouth, and then inserts a finger, or two fingers, and pulls it with them.
And if the mother's mouth is constricted by a hot abscess that has befallen it, then it should not be disturbed. Instead, a discharge of fatty, moist substances should be administered beforehand. And administer plasters; and keep the patient in waters that soften and moisten.
And if the fetus is on its side, then if possible, let it be turned; and what we have said about a living fetus should be administered.
And if that is not possible, then it should be cut into pieces and extracted.
And it is necessary that you not leave any cause within the afterbirth.
And when you have completed all your operation, then administer what we have said about the treatment of boils which occur in the mother.
And if a flow of blood occurs, then put them in astringent waters and administer the other treatment.
And I have already seen a woman in whose womb a stillbirth had occurred, and shortly thereafter pregnant again, and shortly after that, another stillbirth occurred. A long time ago, a boil occurred near his navel; and it swelled until it was opened, and began to discharge pus.
And I was called to treat him, and medicated him for a long time, and the wound was not healed.
Then I applied some strongly adhesive plaster to him, and a bone came out of him, and after a few days, another bone came out; and I was greatly amazed, as there are no bones inside the belly.
And then I thought they were bones from the stillborn child.
Then I continued treating the wound, and extracted many bones from him. The woman, being in her right state of health, and having lived in this condition for a long time, recovered a little from the illness.
And I did not consider this to be strange, but rather that this is knowledge and assistance to what the skilled physician provides with his hands in administering treatment.
Of the forms of instruments necessary for extracting the fetus.
A method of turning with which the mother is opened:
This is the form of a clamp in which the books are clasped, with two turns at the two ends of two rods. However, this turning needs to be more subtle than a clamp, and should be made either of ivory or of a piece of wood.
And the width of each rod should be two fingers, and the margin of each two fingers, and the length of each is one and a half palms; and in the middle of the two rods there are two attachments of the same rod, which are already fixed, whose length is half a palm and a little more, and the width of each is about two fingers, or a little more.
And these two attachments are inserted into the mouth of the mother so that it is opened by them when you turn the two prescribed turns.
Another similar form, even more subtle and lighter:
It should be made of ivory or wood, resembling forceps. However, at its extremity there are two attachments like those previously described, and the length of those attachments is about one palm, and the width of each is two fingers.
And when you want to open the mother with them, then you have the woman lie on the bed with her feet hanging down, her legs spread apart. And then open your hand with the instrument, as if using scissors, to the extent desired, according to the opening of the mother's mouth, until the midwife does what you want.
The form of vertigo, which the ancients described:
A form of pushing with which the fetus is pushed:
A form of bonding/connection with which the large head is contained.
And it resembles forceps, having teeth at the end, as is often the case.  Sometimes it is made long like forceps, in this form, as often happens.  It has teeth like saw teeth, with which it is incised and contained. A form of slight connection/bonding.
A form of a hook having a spine/point.
A form of a hook having two spines/points.
A form of spatula with two ends, with which the head is severed.
A form of two wide spatulas.
All those instruments are used, and the more the species of them are multiplied and prepared by the artisans, the lighter their operation is and the more beneficial to men for their quantity.
And do not neglect those instruments, wherever they may be needed by you, for the necessity of them is not excusable.
Of the extraction of the second tooth.
When the second tooth is retained during childbirth, then you should command the patient to hold their breath, and then make them sneeze with a stimulus, and press your hand on their mouth and nose. If by this the tooth is extracted, good.
And if not, then you take a bowl, pierce a hole in its cover, and place inside it herbs – chamomile, rue, anise, camomile, and Arabic cicada, cassia wood, and St. John's wort – opening the mother's mouth, as is appropriate. All these herbs, or some of them, should be submerged in water in the bowl, and place that over the fire.
And then place a reed cannula in the mother's mouth, and hold it there until the vapor reaches the mother's cavity.
And then make her sneeze as we said, and the second tooth will be forcefully expelled.
However, if this treatment remains ineffective and the tooth is not removed, then instruct the midwife to immerse her left hand in sesame oil or marshmallow extract, and then insert it into the socket and gently search for the tooth with it.  Once located, carefully pull it out gradually.  If the tooth is lodged deep within the gum, then insert her hand as previously described, and when the tooth is found, extract it slowly and gently to avoid causing excessive pain to the mother. Beforehand, it is necessary for the tooth to be moved from side to side with ease.
And if the mother's mouth is constricted, we have already described the treatment with sneezing and herbal poultices.
However, if it has not been expelled by all the methods we have described, be careful not to further irritate it by repeated attempts to remove it.  Instead, whatever is lodged in the mother's mouth should be placed on the woman's thigh, and then treat it with unguent and tetrapharmacon; this will cause it to decompose over a few days, eventually dissolving and being expelled.
But when it decomposes, a foul odor rises to the head and stomach, distressing the patient; and then fumigations and appropriate remedies must be administered.
However, some of the ancients had already tested fumigations using dried nard and figs.
Method of instrument with which the woman is fumigated for retention of menstrual blood and the afterbirth:
It should be made of glass or earthenware.
And the narrow end should be placed in the cone, and the wider end above the fire, and the fumigation should be placed on the embers of the fire.
And let her maintain it until the fumigation is consumed and then make another.
Treatment of the unperforated anus of the child.
Many children are born with unperforated anuses, which are very narrow and obstructed. Therefore, the midwife should perforate that narrowing with her finger; and if not, then perforate it with a sharp instrument, and be careful not to touch the sphincter.
And then place over it wool soaked in wine and oil; and then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
But if you fear it is obstructed, then place a tube into the opening for several days, and remove it when the child is ready to swallow.
And sometimes anal obstruction occurs due to the consolidation of a plague or an abscess; then that consolidation must be incised, and then treated with what we have said about the cure and the use of lead.
Of the treatment of the fistulas that subsequently appear.
The fistulas that develop in the lower area, swollen and thickened, which appear near the anus externally or in the area of one side.
And it is a fistula or abscesses.
And when that swelling is longstanding and is caused by watery white moisture or subtle putrefaction, and sometimes these fistulas are penetrating.
And those penetrating ones are known for what comes out of them through discharge and by the windiness; and sometimes the patient uses discharge, and often worms come out from them.
And sometimes these fistulas penetrate into the bladder, and into the urethra; and some of those penetrating ones go into the joint of the thigh and into the bone marrow of the thigh.
And the way a penetrating fistula is recognized, compared to a non-penetrating one in the anus, is that you insert your index finger into the anus, and carefully insert a small probe of ram's horn or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
But if there is a twisting in it, then insert a thin probe of lead or horsehair into it until you feel the probe or hair against your finger.
And if you don't feel any of that at all, and no discharge, worms, or gas comes from the opening, as we have said, then know that it is not penetrating, and then your efforts should turn to treatment.
And when the fistula penetrates the bladder or the urethra, the sign of it is urination from that area and the prohibition of it until the place is healed with medicine.
But if it is penetrating into the joint or bone, causing pain in the surrounding area, then the sign of it is that the probe passes into it if there is no twisting into the bone, and pain in the surrounding area; and that there is often a prolonged illness; and that treatment there is not effective, nor is it healed with ointment.
And in all those penetrating fistulas there is no complete cure, and the cure of those is the hard work and vanity of learned physicians upon which you must rely.
But in that which is not penetrating and not old, healing with iron is hoped for, as I tell you, and this I have already tested.
And it is necessary that the patient lie between your hands on their back, and raise their legs upwards, with the thighs bent towards their stomach, and then carefully insert a lead probe, or an iron one if there is a twist in the fistula, until you know the spot where the probe penetrates.
And if the pain is around the anus, then it is necessary for you to insert your finger into the anus.
And if, when inserting your finger, you feel the probe already penetrating itself, or if you feel something between your finger and that tissue or flesh, then be certain that it is penetrating; and so do not work on that, for there is no healing in that, as we have said.
But however, some might say that it is cured in some men slowly.
And the treatment by which recovery is expected in this case is that you apply a thin heated cautery, according to the width of the fistula, as previously described, and introduce it into the fistula until it reaches around the anus; and then repeat this two or three times, until you know that all the flesh around the fistulous opening, which resembles the hollow of a bird's feather, has been cauterized.
And then treat it with some bandages until all the cauterized flesh has healed, and then treat it with healing and strengthening medicines; and if it is healed, it is good; and if not, then it will not be healed in any time by any other treatment.
And if the probe enters, and does not penetrate inside your finger that is in the anus, and between that and the probe there is a thick layer of flesh or tissue, and the fistula is on the surface of the anus, then cut the anus at the beginning of the fistula, and cut with the probe; and let it be in the fistula until the incision reaches the place where the tip of the probe reaches, and through the probe it is released and removed.
And then cleanse those fistulous tissues, which are gathered like a bird's feather quill, so that no cause remains.
However, if blood flows between you and your procedure when you cauterize that flesh, then the best and easiest instrument is to cauterize with fire or with a sharp medicine, because cauterization with fire has two good effects: it burns the cauterized tissues, and it stops the blood flow and removes the moisture.
And then treat it with bandages or a linen compress until the area heals, and then treat the wound with ointments that strengthen and heal the flesh.
And these medicines, which have astringent and drying properties; when it is restored, it is already healed and you do not fear a recurrence.
However, if the fistula extends to the anus and is far from the body's surface, then insert your finger into the anus and investigate with it.
And therefore, if you feel resistance, and between you and it there is a membrane or flesh, and it is close to penetration, then there is no operation there, but rather, it should be treated with hope and trust.
This condition can be treated in one of three ways: either cauterize it as we have said; or cut it until you reach its cavity, so that you can introduce remedies and achieve a cure; and do not cut too deeply, lest you injure the surrounding tissues, and thus cause harm to the patient unintentionally; and then treat it with what we have said, for it will be easily healed; or else, remove the membrane and cleanse the pus, cutting it back toward the anus as we have said, either with a probe or another instrument with a sharp tip, and then remove the fistula tissues that are within the incision, after which you can use a scab to help the healing; and then strive to restore the entire wound with cuts, and if the opening above is not healed and the fistula remains open in the anal area, it will be easier for the patient. And sometimes the fistula is treated in this way: when you insert the probe into the fistula, and it is located in the folds of the anus near the body's surface, and at the edge of the anus, then take a probe with a sharp tip, which is similar to a needle, prepared in this manner:
and insert it into that, wrapped in five or so threads; and then insert the threaded probe into the fistula until it reaches the cavity.
However, if it is penetrating near the edge of the anus, then you remove the thread from that opening as if you were inserting your finger into the anus; and you pull out the thread's end and join the two ends together, tightening each one.  Leave it like this for a day or two, and when you cut the thread into the flesh, firmly grasp it until the tissues between the two ends of the thread are cut and fall away.
And then treat the wound until it is healed and sound.
But if the fistula's opening is not penetrating, then make it penetrate, in whatever manner you are prepared, but not too deeply in the region, for you must not cut into the tendons; and then treat it until it is healed.
The shape of the probe used to open the fistula: one curved end is very sharp, and the other part is blunt, so you don't cut what's unnecessary, as sometimes happens.
Of the suturing of hemorrhoids in which blood flows in the incision of those.
Hemorrhoids come in two ways, for either they are like lumps within the anus, as if made of knots, or they are like bunches of grapes. And they are small or large, and the blood flows from them constantly, and they are single or multiple, and they are outside the anus, and at the extremities of it.
However, those outside the anus are according to the periods of less moisture, from which yellow water or a little blood with a continuous flow comes, and it is according to the colour of the flow.
And the treatment of those inside the anus is that you should tell the patient to sit down and press until the anus opens and the hemorrhoids appear to you. Then you hold and lift them with tweezers or your fingernails, and then cut them away from their roots.
But if the tweezers are not holding them due to their moisture and softness, then take them with a rough cloth, or cotton, or wool strips, and pull them out with your fingers, and then cut them, and sprinkle some hot powders over their incisions, so that they will be like cauterization; or cauterize them, according to what is preceded in the chapter on cauterization. And then treat them with another treatment until they are healed.
And if the anus does not yield to evacuation, then prick the patient with a cautery in which there is a small bite, and wash it with whatever is inside the anus, so that it yields to evacuation easily when the patient is squeezed.
But if the hemorrhoids are outside the anus, then the cause is slight, and you should grasp them with your fingernail, or tweezers, and cut them, and then treat them with what we have said until they are healed.
And for those you have cut, you should apply stitches to them in this manner: take a thread wrapped around, insert it into a needle, then pull the hemorrhoids apart, and pierce it with the needle into the root of the other part, and wrap both ends of the thread in the portion below the needle, and do it latitudinally; and tighten the hemorrhoid with a strong bandage, then tie the thread and remove the needle.
And do this to all of them, and leave one of them unsewn, so that the excess blood will flow from it.
And then place a cloth soaked in heated oil or ointment on the anus; place it over the area and tell the patient to rest. And then leave it until it falls out; and when it has fallen out, treat them with ointments or other remedies until healed.
And when they are old and no longer respond to that treatment, then you must scrape them with the tip of a spatula or your fingernail until they are moist and the crust of pus on top, which prevents healing, is removed; and then treat them until they are healed.
Then scrape them with a more forceful scraping than the first, until they bleed and are raw; and then treat them until they are healed.
Know that alamermar, this is the key, and it is nothing but a red spot, like a small nailhead, according to the colour of the body, and it is found throughout the body, especially in the parts below the feet and in the joints, and it is indicative of that disease's affliction.
Then it is necessary to cut out that which is around the spot, using shears or forceps, and to remove it from its root; and then treat that area.
And if you wish, cauterize it according to what is described in its chapter.
But a wart is a small, rough, fistulated, round elevation on the surface of the body, and it often appears on the hands of children.
And its treatment is to scrape or cut it, or to squeeze it with a file or a needle until it breaks. And if you wish, cauterize it, as we have said, with fire or with a sharp medicine.
But a pimple is a small, festered or fistulous, large elevation on the surface of the body, often found on the groin.  When the cold touches it, it feels like an ant bite, and it forms around the body.
And the treatment is to take a hollow tube made from a hawk's or vulture's feather, strong, and place it over the pimple until the tube encircles the pimple's edges.  Then, twist your hand with the tube until you cut through what is within the pimple's circle, and place it on the flesh around it, eradicating the pimple from its root.
And if you wish, do this with a tube of bronze or iron, following this method:
The part above the tube should be slender, closed (that is, not pierced), wrapped so that the grip on it is firm and its rotation smooth.
And if you want to cauterize the pimple, do so as previously described in the section on cauterizing ulcers in the chapter on cauterization.

Of the treatment of plagues.
I have already said in the division of the treatment of plagues what was appropriate for the book, and I say thus the treatment of them with hands and with medicines according to the progression.
Therefore, I say that plagues are diverse depending on how they are caused and according to the place where the plague occurs.
And the causes for which plagues are often caused are thus: throwing of stones, or cutting with a sword or knife, or hitting with a spear, or with a stick, or with an arrow, or similar to those of many causes.
But the plagues that are in the places of the body are like a plague that falls on the head, or the neck, or the feet, or the belly, or the liver, and similar to those of the limbs.
And I am recounting the treatment of some plagues so that you may apply that reasoning and rule to other plagues.
And I will begin with the simple plagues of the head, for the memory of the compound ones will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
Therefore, I say that when a simple plague occurs on the head, and it is not a fracture, then consider: if it is from the throwing of a stone or similar, and it has only broken the skin and is a large wound, and you fear the onset of a hot abscess in that patient, then you should quickly bleed from the cephalic vein, and do not delay this; and draw from him the blood according to his strength, if no other cause prevents bloodletting, especially if the blood that has come out of the wound is little.
And let the bloodletting be on the opposite side of the affected part; and guard the patient from repletion and from strong foods and drinks.
But if some cause prohibits bloodletting, then lessen the patient's intake of food and do not allow him near meat or wine.
And if a hot abscess occurs on the wound, apply a cloth steeped in warmed oil, or in wine in which a styptic has been soaked, to the wound.
But if a hot abscess is certain, then apply to the wound, if it is recent, its own blood, and if the air hasn't changed that powder which I shall tell you about shortly.
And if the air has already altered it, then apply some ointments until it is healed.
But if the wound is large, or from a cut or similar injury, and its edges are not brought together by sutures, then bring those together with sutures, as I will explain concerning their suture.
However, if the wound has already exposed the bone and tendon, and there is no retention but a small suspension, then cut that, and then cure the wound with medicines and restore the flesh there, instead of codena, and command the patient to eat foods rich in fat: heads of various animals, and other similar parts, until it is complete.
And if you find putrefaction in the flesh and it does not adhere to the bone, then you cut away all the putrid material and throw it away, and then treat it.
But if in these wounds there is an artery or vein from which blood flow may result, and it is not severed by medicines, then you investigate the artery, and if you find it not severed, then you sever it with a spatula, or tie it; and if necessity compels you that what we have said does not work, then you cauterize until the blood flow is stopped.
And if these wounds are simple and small, then their cause is slight; therefore, you can sprinkle this powder over them, for it will consolidate them before the air changes them.
And the method for the powder is this: take one part of olive oil, two parts of dragon's blood, and three parts of unburnt resin; let all be finely ground and sifted, and then fill the wound with it, and bind it firmly until it adheres well to it and is coagulated by the blood.
And then you bandage it with dressings and leave it, and do not remove them until it is healed, for the medicine will not be effective until it is completely healed.
And sometimes this works alone, when you do not have frankincense and dragon's blood readily available.
And you perform this same operation on large wounds when it is appropriate to apply it, and they are tightly bound, and for fresh wounds with their own blood, which the air has not altered.
And if the air has altered them, and especially when it is summertime, then this powder application is not appropriate, but rather treat them with what we have previously described, or apply digestive ointments, or a powder made from barley flour mixed with water and honey until it forms a paste; and then treat them with the other method until they are healed.
But if, by chance, the wound is accompanied by a fractured bone, and it is small, then you extract it with a gentle action.
And I will describe the treatment for head fractures in what follows.
Of wounds of the neck.
However, if the wound happens on the neck, there is no difference in treatment, and it is treated similarly to a simple wound of the head.
However, if the neck wound involves an incised nerve or artery, if it's a nerve,  it shouldn't be treated with anything that causes strong astringency, like zinc or verdigris (which is vitriol) and similar things, because they harm the nerves and resist healing. And do not apply anything excessively cold to the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest of all the limbs.
And if it is treated with mild remedies, such as washing the wound with fresh water, sometimes infused in oil (whether it has been processed or not), and applying poultices when washing it with fresh water, and other similar medicinal stones according to this method, and moist ointments.
But if the wound is large, then administer sutures, or stitch the edges together, and then treat it with powders until it heals.
But if the wound is deep or extends to the lowermost part of the tissue, then pierce it in the deepest place.
But if an artery is already cut in the wound and blood is flowing, then either tie it off, or cauterize it if necessary.
But if the vertebrae of the neck or the entire spine have been cut and the neck veins are saved, then you should stitch the edges of the spinal column together along the spine and do not touch it; initially straighten it and return it to its natural position, then tightly secure it with proper bandages, and leave it for some days.  Then treat it with ointments that are styptic and supportive until it is healed.
But if the wound has already reached the bone, treat it. Then, if there are bone fragments in it, remove all you can; and what you cannot remove, leave it until the wound can fester and separate, and the discharge is lessened.
And if the wound is recent, then sprinkle the powder recommended to you over it. But if a fistula has formed in the wound, then treat it with what is mentioned in its corresponding chapter.
If it is a wound from a spear or knife, and you see how deep it is, then consider if the wound is becoming more inflamed when the patient weakens; if so, understand that the wound is fatal.
And if it is not deep, and the wound is recent, with its own blood, then in the first hour you put powder on it, and do not press it so that the blood is not trapped deep inside and returns to the heart and kills the patient, but put an attractive ointment there, and remove it twice a day.
And if the ointment is not available to you, then place old lint over the wound opening to absorb any moisture; and have the patient sleep on the wound to allow any accumulated matter to drain out.
However, if three days or more have passed since the wound, and the patient shows no spasms, tremors, or heart distress, or other bad conditions, then understand that the wound is healing; and then treat it with poultices and other appropriate remedies until healed.
But if the healing of the wound is delayed, and it remains open for a long time, then understand that a fistula has already formed; treat it then according to its specific treatment method.
And if the wound is from a cut with a knife or sword, and is superficial on the foot or back, then treat it with stitches if it's large, or with powder if it's small.
But if the injury has already penetrated the bone, and some pieces of bone have been severed, then you should clean the wound and attempt to remove those pieces if they are loose. But if they are not loose, then leave them until the wound can heal, as removing them will cause pain.
And for other wounds affecting other limbs, the method of treatment is the same as what we have already described.
Of wounds of the abdomen.
The ailment affecting the abdomen is either severe, mild, or moderate.
And a small rupture is difficult to repair in another way, and the reduction of them is even more difficult if the intestines are not returned to their place promptly, for if it opens and becomes swollen, the insertion of it is made difficult.
Therefore, the best rupture is moderate, for in that case the reduction of the intestines is not difficult, as it is in the two aforementioned types.
And know that the suturing of the abdomen is done in four ways, but two of these sutures are common to those used for other wounds on the body.
And two other sutures, though similar to those used on other wounds, are nonetheless more specific to abdominal sutures.
And I will explain each to you with exposition and declaration.
So I say that when the wound is small and some part of the intestines has protruded through it, and it is difficult to return it, this can happen in one of two ways: either due to the small size of the rupture, as we have said, or when the intestines have become inflamed due to the coldness of the air.
And so when this is the case, you should warm the area by soaking a sponge or damp cloth in warm water alone, or in water with stinging nettles, cyperus, and spikenard, and apply this to the intestine until the inflammation subsides.
And sometimes, using water with astringents is better than plain water for resolving the inflammation.
And when you see the inflammation subsiding, then moisten the intestine with water in which mullein and mallows have been boiled, for this will ease his internal suffering with little effort.
But if the internal suffering is relieved by this treatment, then gently dissect the rupture a little with an instrument used for hemorrhoids.
And the first treatment is better, when it's appropriate and doesn't involve cutting, and there is no need to dry it out or cause weakness.
Of the instrument, describe its shape:
One part of it is sharply curved, and the other part is not sharp, and the end is thin, but not as thin as a spatula; rather, it is a little blunt.
And therefore, if the wound is aggravated and the intestine is outside, then its reduction should be according to its natural shape, in its proper place, if possible, because that is better.
But when the rupture is wide, and is in the lower part of the abdomen, then you should have the patient lie on their back, and raise their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the upper part of the abdomen, then you should raise the head and feet higher than the lower parts.
And similarly, if the rupture is in one of the two parts of the abdomen, then always keep your attention and consideration focused on this, so that the part where the wound is located is higher than the other.
And thus you should administer this in both large and smaller wounds.
And in small wounds, place what you have prepared, and then have the assistant hold the rupture entirely with their hand and close the edges together, and then determine the cause of any further sutures needed.
And this is the common method of suturing: take a needle, or needles according to the size of the wound; then place the tip of the needle at the edge of the rupture on the ring finger, and thread the needle through, or otherwise you do not place the thread in the two ends of the opening, with the two ends of the thread underneath the opening to bring them together; and you have now joined the two ends of the opening and the two ends of the thread, making four stitches.
Then tie with double thread around the needle, and sometimes from two sides together, and then close the two edges and the wound with a proper closure; and then leave the thickness of a finger and insert another needle there, and then tie it with thread in the same way as the first needle; and do not stop doing this if necessary with the needles until you have completed the entire closure of the wound.
And the needles should be of medium thickness, neither too fine nor too thick; for fine needles easily pierce the flesh; and thick ones are difficult to thread, and therefore they should be of medium thickness.
And the needle should not be placed too close to the two ends of the opening, so that the flesh is not pierced easily and the wound opens up before its healing.
And the sutures should not be prolonged, so that the wound is not prevented from healing.
And then cut the ends of the needles so that they do not bother the patient during their sleep; and place spread powders on the suture from all sides, holding the ends of the needles; and leave them until you know the wound is already healed.
And this method of suturing with needles is most suitable for small wounds, because one or two needles, or thereabouts, are sufficient for their closure.
However, the second suture is a standard one: and it is that you close the four edges, of the opening, and the two edges of the cut, all at once, with a needle of a fidelity, size, and fineness suitable for the task.
And then, when you have pierced these four edges with the needle, withdraw the needle from the same place you started, so that the thread retracts from the most superior part to the wound, so that the suture is like a cloth stitch, as when cloths are joined.
And place between each stitch the thickness of the little finger.
And this suture is known to men (or, and this suture is known by men).
And with this suture, I closed the wound that had befallen a man in his belly, who had been wounded with a knife, and the rupture of the wound was more than a palm in length, and the intestines had protruded about two palms from the middle part and the rupture was in the middle of the limb; and then I rejoined that part after the intestines had been outside the wound for twenty-four hours.
And the wound was consolidated within fifteen days or thereabouts, and I cured him, and he is healed; and after this, he lived for many years, and he is recovered in his condition.
And other physicians had judged that he would not be healed; and by a miracle, it was, for I did not cure him with ointments, for it was in a place where no ointment or medicine was to be found, but I placed old linen on the wound twice a day and continuously washed it with honey water until he was healed.
But I will tell you two kinds of sutures, proper according to the account of Paraula.
And it is that you begin with a suture of the cord, and you insert the needle from the outside to the inside.
And so, as the needle penetrates the cord and in that same laceration, following its straight and length along the whole body, and leave the end of the thread where you have inserted the needle; and make the needle penetrate from the inside to the outside at the other end of the slit.
And when you have made that penetrate, then you make it penetrate again into that same slit of the wound from the outside to the inside; and leave the end of the thread that is in this loop, and make the needle penetrate the other end of the wound from the inside to the outside.
And make that penetration with the penetration that you make the thread enter the wound at the end of the wound, which is on the part towards him until all that penetrates.
And then begin on this same side and stitch that with the end of the thread on the other side, and remove the needle from the cord which it penetrated, and then return that into that cord and stitch the end of the thread that is on the other side with this end of the wound; and remove that from the cord that is on the side of him.
And do this once and again, and do this one time then another time until you sew all of that which is outside according to that example.
And the sum of this manner of suturing is that you sew with the suturing of hides, with which you sew the hides, so that you sew the thread once from the side of the end of the cord, and that you leave that again until you have completed it.
But the second species of suture, which is also called Gaulish, and this is spoken of by him and recounted by him, is that you stitch it in a similar manner to how some medical practitioners stitch it, in such a way that they join each part to its corresponding part to him according to nature; and they apply the end of one to him and the end of the wound to the other end of him, and this is done according to what I have recounted to you.
You must place the needle into the end of the wound close to the outside part, and have it penetrate to the inside part of that same place, and leave both ends of the thread; and then turn the needle and have it penetrate from outside to inside at both ends of the thread.
And then turn each of those, and have each one penetrate from the inside part to the outside part at the two ends of the wound, other than those on the opposite side.
And this manner of suturing is better than the common, superficial suturing, and it is the suturing of which the previous recollection has spoken.
This is the Gaulish method/teaching.

And know that when the rupture is in the middle part of the belly, then its suturing is more difficult than in other parts of the belly.

And if pain or putrefaction is felt in their intestines, as often happens, then cauterize it with strong black wine, especially if the ulcer has reached the intestine and has made a penetrating exit into its cavity.

But if the wound is large and extensive, especially if it's in one of the delicate intestines, because then there is no true cure but merely a mitigation, and not a complete healing.
Of the treatment of ulcers and fistulas.
Know that any wound or abscess that becomes old and chronic, and develops into an ulcer that does not heal and constantly discharges pus and is not surgically removed, then, wherever it may be on the body, is universally called a fistula, and we call it an ulcer.
And a fistula, in truth, is a hard, white, fibrous growth that causes no pain, and has a cavity like the cavity of a bird's nest; and for this reason we call that ulcer a "rized" ulcer, that is, a nest.
And in some people it is moist, which discharges pus; and often the moisture is discharged in a few hours. And sometimes this moisture is thick, and sometimes thin, and sometimes large, and sometimes subtle.
I have already shown all those causes, and the signs of them and their treatment with medicines in the division.
And it is necessary that I make you aware of the treatment of a fistula which is caused by surgical means using the hands.
And know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for some of them reach the large veins and arteries, or the nerves, or the spine, or the intestines, or the bladder, or some of the ribs, or some of the vertebrae of the back, or some of the joints formed by composition, such as those of the hand and foot; and those that occur near the main part of the limb and similar structures.
Therefore, those fistulas of this type are among the illnesses with difficult healing, and do not receive a cure, and dealing with them is a labour and a display of ignorance.
And if any of the fistulas is not deep enough to reach these locations I have mentioned, and you hope and trust in its treatment, and wish to achieve understanding of it, then take a probe or iron, and if the fistula is running in a straight line, explore it with that.
But if the fistula is winding, then investigate it with a probe of fine lead, for lead, due to its light weight, is more easily turned towards and follows the winding path.
And if the fistula has many horrors (i.e., is very complicated), it is not possible for you to make a diagnosis using a probe.
Then irrigate the openings with its openings, for the moisture with which you irrigate it will flow towards the other openings and run from them.
Then carefully inquire, in whatever way you can, to see if there are bones or nerves, and if the fistula's cavity is distant or near, or if it is a fistula with many openings and you are examining all of it with your full strength, with your questioning, with which you question the patient, and the discovery of the pain through your pressing with your hand on the spot, and similar to the indications and accidental causes of an abscess.
And when you have established all those things with true judgment, then proceed to the cure according to your knowledge: and you must consider then if it is a superficial, close fistula, or in a saline location, distant from a joint, or from a nerve, or artery, or vein, or one of the locations which I have told you.
Then you dry the fistula according to what was previously said in the description of it, and remove whatever is in that filtration and decaying flesh, and whatever has grown in the opening of the flesh, or of pus and the like, and treat it until it is healed.
But if the fistula is of deep origin, and is properly ascertained, then it must be incised as much as possible, and afterwards cleanse it of all its corrupt flesh. Then apply some bandages containing sharp medicaments, and place those inside the cavity of the fistula, which you have opened with an iron instrument.
And do this repeatedly until the sharp medicine corrodes all that remains within the fistula's cavity of corruption.
And then restore it with ointments that generate healthy flesh until it is healed.
But if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it according to what we have described.
But if the cause of the fistula is bone, and you are certain of this, then you shall probe and dry it as we have described, provided you do not impede any vein, nerve, or principal member as we have stated.
But if the bone is exposed and has some corruption or blackness, then you should scrape away this corruption until it is entirely removed; then heal it with something that causes flesh to grow until it is healed.
And if it is not healed and still bleeds as before, then know that you have not fully eradicated the corruption; therefore, you shall expose it a second time, carefully scrape and cleanse it thoroughly with your strongest tools, and then restore it.
And if it is healed, well and good; but if not, then know that the corruption is in a deeply hidden part of the body, which cannot be reached, and then you have no choice but to leave it be.
And if the corrupted bone is small, or it is possible for you to remove it, then you should remove it with delicate forceps suitable for this purpose.
And if there are many bones, then meticulously remove all of them, and leave no trace of them with your strength.
But if any difficulty arises from the humors, and there is no fear or error in their incision, then cut those ligaments or flesh, if present, and free the bones.
But if you are not prepared to remove the bones at once, then place something over the wound that can cover it, and leave it until the area around those bones of flesh and ligaments is free, and keep the wound from healing, and keep the incision you made in your operation from closing up.
However, if you fear, place on it cotton soaked in bruised olive oil, or cotton soaked in Egyptian unguent, or in any of the green ointments, for when those ligaments soften and the bones are separated from them, the removal, and the extraction of them, is eased.
But if it is a large bone, such as a leg bone or thigh bone, or similar, and only the surface of it is corrupted, then scrape that with a rasp until that blackness and corruption is removed, and then close the wound.
But if the corrupted part is large, and the corruption has already reached the marrow of the bone, then it is necessary to cut that, and cut all the way to where the corruption has reached, and then treat that until it is healed.
And I tell you what happened to a man in his thigh, so that you can use this as an example and help in your operation.
There was a young man, about 30 years old, who suffered pain in his thigh.  And from the parts within, the disease spread through the body until it reached the thigh.  It was a matter of abscess, with a large abscess, and not an external cause.
And then the time was prolonged by the error of the doctors until the abscess opened, and many materials came out.  Its cure was nearly abandoned until the leg became fistulous, and many openings formed, which all discharged pus and bodily humors.
And then many doctors treated him for about two years, and none of them were skilled in the art, until I was called.
And I saw his leg and the materials that flowed from those openings, through great parts; and the man's body was already wasted away, and its color was yellow.
And then I inserted a probe into one of those openings, and the probe reached the bone.
And I, quickly probing all the openings, found them extending from all parts of the leg.
And then I probed and incised one of those openings until I exposed a portion of the bone, and found it corrupted, already decayed and blackened; and a part of the leg was already corrupted, having penetrated to the marrow.
And then I sealed what I had uncovered and prepared of the exposed bone.
And I concluded that it was not in the bone, but that corruption which I had excised and sealed, and I had already cured it.
And then I applied restorative medicines to the wound for a long time, but it did not heal.
And then I again probed and uncovered the bone, over the previous exposure, and found continued corruption alongside the bone.
And I sealed what appeared to me of that corruption, and then I was forced to perform its treatment and restoration, but it was not restored.
And then I uncovered it again and did not cease to cut into the bone little by little, specifically, forcing its restoration.  It was not restored until I cut around a palm's width of it, and extracted its marrow.  Then I restored it with medicines, and it is slightly consolidated and healed.
And further operations and incisions on it are not necessary, except for the weakness of the patient, and the patient's low tolerance and fear of death, because in such cases, fainting fits, or bad syncopes, occur at all hours due to excess evacuation.
And thus, it is healed completely, and there is nothing in place of the bone but hard flesh; and its condition in the body is now good, and its virtue returned; and it is restored to its proper functions and experiences no difficulty walking or in any other activity.
However, if the bone is protruding from the body, then you must cut it with this method:  take a bandage and tightly bind it to the end of that protruding bone, and instruct someone to pull it outward.  Then place a thicker wool bandage over the first one; and then tie this over the flesh that is beneath the bone, and pull the extremity so that it pulls the flesh inward, and you expose the flesh at the spot you want to cut so the cut does not damage the flesh.
And place a piece of wood or a board beneath the bone properly, for when you do this, the cut is not prevented from cutting the corrupted flesh.
And the cut should be made slowly over the decayed area, for if the decay is in the cavity of the bone and does not show in its surface, you may have to make another incision.
And if the bone is decayed but not protruding, and one part is continuous with the other, and the decay is in the middle or a portion of it, then you must expose the flesh completely on all sides; and then place wood beneath, and then cut from the first section where the decay is until the incision is extended to the other part.
And let the incision be precisely over the area of decay, as we have said.
And if the decay is in the joint, cut into that decayed joint and saw the bone where it is connected to the other part.
And if the decay is in the continuation of two joints, then it is not a rational, but rather an ingenious, problem.
And if the decay is in the wrist or ankle, it is very difficult; however, you must investigate the decay in whatever way it appears to you, and expose it, and clean it according to any possible arrangement, and with every ingenious means, be rectified, as long as you do not encounter a vein or nerve.
And know that the incisions and saws for cutting these bones are very much dependent on the position of the bones, and their preparation, their thickness, their subtlety, their size, their smallness, their hardness, and their rarity; therefore, you must prepare instruments appropriate for each type of operation.
And know that this operation signifies to you the type of instrument you need; when great study, length of experience, and knowledge of the techniques of this art, and experience with illnesses, are yours, then you will already know what instruments are appropriate for each ailment.
